     <p>Brown ranked 5th in the country in <a href="/wiki/Newsweek" title="Newsweek">Newsweek</a>/<a href="/wiki/The_Daily_Beast" title="The Daily Beast">The Daily Beast</a>'s &quot;America's Brainiac Schools&quot;. The rankings are calculated based on the number of prestigious scholarships, adjusted for population size, won by students, including <a href="/wiki/Rhodes_Scholarship" title="Rhodes Scholarship">Rhodes Scholarships</a>, <a href="/wiki/Truman_Scholarship" title="Truman Scholarship" class="mw-redirect">Truman Scholarships</a>, <a href="/wiki/Marshall_Scholarship" title="Marshall Scholarship">Marshall Scholarships</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gates_Scholarship" title="Gates Scholarship">Gates Scholarships</a> (since 2001), and the number of students receiving <a href="/wiki/Fulbright_scholarship" title="Fulbright scholarship" class="mw-redirect">Fulbright scholarships</a> (since 1993). Also factored in are scores on admissions tests, admission rates, and the proportion of students in the top 10% of their graduating high school class. The 4 schools besting Brown were, in order of rank, <a href="/wiki/Yale_University" title="Yale University">Yale University</a>, <a href="/wiki/Princeton_University" title="Princeton University">Princeton University</a>, <a href="/wiki/Harvard_University" title="Harvard University">Harvard University</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Stanford_University" title="Stanford University">Stanford University</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79"><span>[</span>79<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>As it had in 2007 and 2010, the 2011 <a href="/wiki/Princeton_Review" title="Princeton Review" class="mw-redirect">Princeton Review</a> email poll of college students ranked Brown 1st in the country for &quot;Happiest Students.&quot;<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80"><span>[</span>80<span>]</span></a></sup> Brown is 3rd in the country (tied with <a href="/wiki/Stanford_University" title="Stanford University">Stanford</a>) in the number of students awarded Fulbright grants, according to the October 2010 ranking compiled by the <i>Chronicle of Higher Education</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81"><span>[</span>81<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>Graduate programs that ranked the top 10 in the 2010 <a href="/wiki/US_News_%26_World_Report" title="US News &amp; World Report" class="mw-redirect">US News &amp; World Report</a> graduate school rankings included applied mathematics at 5th<sup id="cite_ref-rankingsandreviews1_50-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rankingsandreviews1-50"><span>[</span>50<span>]</span></a></sup> and growth economics at 8th.<sup id="cite_ref-rankingsandreviews4_62-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rankingsandreviews4-62"><span>[</span>62<span>]</span></a></sup> Those that are ranked in the top 20 are history at 14th,<sup id="cite_ref-rankingsandreviews3_61-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rankingsandreviews3-61"><span>[</span>61<span>]</span></a></sup> economics at 17th,<sup id="cite_ref-rankingsandreviews5_63-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rankingsandreviews5-63"><span>[</span>63<span>]</span></a></sup> English at 13th,<sup id="cite_ref-rankingsandreviews2_60-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rankingsandreviews2-60"><span>[</span>60<span>]</span></a></sup> engineering at 20th, mathematics at 14th,<sup id="cite_ref-grad-schools.usnews.rankingsandreviews.com_51-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-grad-schools.usnews.rankingsandreviews.com-51"><span>[</span>51<span>]</span></a></sup> and computer science at 20th.<sup id="cite_ref-grad-schools.usnews.rankingsandreviews.com_51-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-grad-schools.usnews.rankingsandreviews.com-51"><span>[</span>51<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Admission_and_financial_aid">Admission and financial aid</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Brown_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Admission and financial aid">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:BrownUniversity-CorlissBrackettHouse.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c7/BrownUniversity-CorlissBrackettHouse.jpg/200px-BrownUniversity-CorlissBrackettHouse.jpg" width="200" height="150" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c7/BrownUniversity-CorlissBrackettHouse.jpg/300px-BrownUniversity-CorlissBrackettHouse.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c7/BrownUniversity-CorlissBrackettHouse.jpg/400px-BrownUniversity-CorlissBrackettHouse.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:BrownUniversity-CorlissBrackettHouse.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf8/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> Corliss Brackett House, Brown's Undergraduate Admissions Office
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>Brown is one of the most selective universities in the world. The admission rate for the undergraduate class of 2015 was 8.7 percent.<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82"><span>[</span>82<span>]</span></a></sup> For the class of 2014, 96 percent of accepted students were in the top 10 percent of their high school class, and 38 percent were either <a href="/wiki/Valedictorian" title="Valedictorian">valedictorian</a> or <a href="/wiki/Salutatorian" title="Salutatorian">salutatorian</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83"><span>[</span>83<span>]</span></a></sup> Brown began using the <a href="/wiki/Common_Application" title="Common Application">Common Application</a> in the Fall of 2008. The Graduate School is also intensely competitive, with graduate programs accepting 18% of the 7,283 students who applied in 2008. The Warren <a href="/wiki/Alpert_Medical_School" title="Alpert Medical School">Alpert Medical School</a> of Brown University accepted less than 2% of more than 5,000 applicants.<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84"><span>[</span>84<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85"><span>[</span>85<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86"><span>[</span>86<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87"><span>[</span>87<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>Brown is <a href="/wiki/Need-blind" title="Need-blind" class="mw-redirect">need-blind</a> for all domestic applicants. Brown's <a href="/wiki/Financial_aid_(educational_expenses)" title="Financial aid (educational expenses)" class="mw-redirect">financial aid</a> policy eliminates loans for all students whose family incomes are under $100,000, as well as all parental contributions for families whose incomes fall under $60,000.<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88"><span>[</span>88<span>]</span></a></sup> For these purposes, income is calculated by summing the adjusted gross income plus all untaxed income. In 2012, the program awarded need-based scholarships worth around $90 million.<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89"><span>[</span>89<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>According to the university, Brown seeks diverse applicants from &quot;all walks of life, backgrounds, interests, and cultural heritages&quot; but has &quot;no quotas of any kind&quot;.<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90"><span>[</span>90<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Campus">Campus</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Brown_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Campus">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <p>Brown is the largest institutional landowner in Providence,<sup id="cite_ref-strat_frame_91-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-strat_frame-91"><span>[</span>91<span>]</span></a></sup> with properties in the East Side and the Jewelry District.<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92"><span>[</span>92<span>]</span></a></sup> Unlike some other schools, there are also no clear physical landmarks to determine where Brown's campus begins or ends.<sup id="cite_ref-strat_frame_91-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-strat_frame-91"><span>[</span>91<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>There is no official designation of different campus areas from the University, but the institution's buildings can be roughly categorized as follows.</p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Main_campus">Main campus</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Brown_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Main campus">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <div class="rellink">
      Further information: 
      <a href="/wiki/List_of_Brown_University_buildings" title="List of Brown University buildings">List of Brown University buildings</a>
     </div> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:BrownUniversity-UniversityHall.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/BrownUniversity-UniversityHall.jpg/220px-BrownUniversity-UniversityHall.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/BrownUniversity-UniversityHall.jpg/330px-BrownUniversity-UniversityHall.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/BrownUniversity-UniversityHall.jpg/440px-BrownUniversity-UniversityHall.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:BrownUniversity-UniversityHall.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf8/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> Built in 1770, 
        <a href="/wiki/University_Hall_(Brown_University)" title="University Hall (Brown University)">University Hall</a> is the oldest building on Brown's campus.
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>Brown's main campus is located on College Hill, in the East Side, across the Providence River from downtown Providence. This is the where the University was relocated in 1770 after it was first established in <a href="/wiki/Warren,_Rhode_Island" title="Warren, Rhode Island">Warren, Rhode Island</a>, in 1764. The main campus consists of 235 buildings and covers 143 acres (0.58&nbsp;km<sup>2</sup>). A salient feature of Brown's campus is that many of the academic departments reside in smaller, Victorian-era houses that the University has acquired over the years from the surrounding neighborhood.</p> 
     <p>The main campus area can be subdivided further into the inner, traditional campus greens and the outer neighborhood. The two greens, the <i>Main Green</i> and <i>Ruth J. Simmons Quadrangle</i> (formerly &quot;Lincoln Field&quot;), are large grass fields perpendicular to each other. These two areas contain many of the larger and more traditional academic and dormitory buildings, including University Hall (1770). This part of the main campus is enclosed by brick and rod iron fence, with the <a href="/wiki/Van_Wickle_Gates" title="Van Wickle Gates">Van Wickle Gates</a> serving as the prominent entrance on College Street. It is this area that is featured in most publications and photographs of Brown's campus.</p> 
     <p>Outside of the gates, but still considered part of the main campus, are other University buildings and libraries that have been built at Brown over the centuries. This includes the <a href="/wiki/List_of_Brown_University_buildings#Wriston_Quadrangle" title="List of Brown University buildings">Wriston Quad</a> to the south of the Main Green; the John Hay Library and John D. Rockefeller, Jr. Library directly across the street from the Van Wickle Gates; and the <a href="/wiki/Sciences_Library_(Brown_University)" title="Sciences Library (Brown University)">Sciences Library</a> and Thomas J. Watson, Sr. Center for Information Technology (CIT) adjacent to the Soldiers Memorial Gate. Because this area is not confined by the gates, Brown has been able to acquire larger plots of land and construct much larger buildings as the University has expanded.</p> 
     <p>Adjacent to Brown's main campus, and further down the Hill to the west by the Providence River, is the campus of the <a href="/wiki/Rhode_Island_School_of_Design" title="Rhode Island School of Design">Rhode Island School of Design</a>. <a href="/wiki/Thayer_Street" title="Thayer Street">Thayer Street</a>, which runs through Brown's campus, is a commercial district that hosts many restaurants and shops popular with students and faculty from Brown and RISD.</p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Pembroke_Campus">Pembroke Campus</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Brown_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Pembroke Campus">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:BrownUniversity-AndrewsHall.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ae/BrownUniversity-AndrewsHall.jpg/220px-BrownUniversity-AndrewsHall.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ae/BrownUniversity-AndrewsHall.jpg/330px-BrownUniversity-AndrewsHall.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ae/BrownUniversity-AndrewsHall.jpg/440px-BrownUniversity-AndrewsHall.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:BrownUniversity-AndrewsHall.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf8/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> Andrews Hall on the Pembroke Campus
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>When <a href="/wiki/Pembroke_College_(Brown_University)" title="Pembroke College (Brown University)" class="mw-redirect">Pembroke College</a> merged with Brown in 1971, the campus was absorbed as part of Brown's overall campus. For the most part, the campus is made up of dormitories, although notable exceptions include: Alumnae Hall, which houses a dance floor and a small University-run diner known as The Gate; Smith-Buonano hall, the gymnasium of Pembroke College that was later renovated to contain a common room, classrooms, and a lecture hall; and Pembroke Hall, the original classroom building for Pembroke College and now home to the Cogut Center for the Humanities and the <a href="/wiki/Pembroke_Center_for_Teaching_and_Research_on_Women" title="Pembroke Center for Teaching and Research on Women">Pembroke Center for Teaching and Research on Women</a>. Furthermore, the campus has its own dining hall, Verney-Woolley Dining Hall, the second of Brown's main dining halls. Somewhere between 25 and 30% of the incoming Freshman class lives on Pembroke, though there are also many upperclassmen.</p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="The_Walk_and_surrounding_area">The Walk and surrounding area</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Brown_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: The Walk and surrounding area">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>The Brown Walk connects Pembroke Campus to the main campus. It's a newer green space, extending north from Waterman Street. It is bordered by the building at 155 Angell St. (home to the Africana Studies Department and the Rites and Reason Theatre) and the UEL (Urban Environmental Lab, a.k.a. The Center for Environmental Studies, also facing Angell St) among other things. Between Pembroke Campus and Main Campus, next to the Brown Bookstore, the Granoff Center for the Creative Arts opened in January 2011.</p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="East_Campus">East Campus</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Brown_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: East Campus">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>The <b>East Campus</b> was originally the main campus location of Brown's former neighbor <a href="/wiki/Bryant_College" title="Bryant College" class="mw-redirect">Bryant College</a>. Brown purchased Bryant's East Side campus in 1969 for $5.0 million when the latter school was moving to a new location. This added 10 acres (40,000&nbsp;m<sup>2</sup>) of land and additional 26 buildings adjacent to the main campus area. The area was officially designated East Campus in 1971.</p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_areas">Other areas</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Brown_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Other areas">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>On the East Side: Also on the Hill, but further to the south and away from the main campus area, is <a href="/wiki/Wickenden_Street" title="Wickenden Street">Wickenden Street</a>, another commercial district offering restaurants and shops. <a href="/wiki/Brown_Stadium" title="Brown Stadium">Brown Stadium</a>, built in 1925 and home to the football team, is located approximately a mile to the northeast of the main campus. Marston Boathouse, the home of the crew teams, lies on the Blackstone/Seekonk River, to the southeast of campus.</p> 
     <p>Elsewhere in Providence: More recently, Brown has expanded into the Jewelry District, located in southern downtown Providence, by acquiring and renovating five buildings to serve as administrative and research facilities.</p> 
     <p>Outside of Providence: Brown also owns a 376-acre (1.52&nbsp;km<sup>2</sup>) property, the Mount Hope Grant, in <a href="/wiki/Bristol,_Rhode_Island" title="Bristol, Rhode Island">Bristol</a>, which is the setting of the <a href="/wiki/Haffenreffer_Museum_of_Anthropology" title="Haffenreffer Museum of Anthropology">Haffenreffer Museum of Anthropology</a>'s Collection Research Center.</p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="John_Hay_Library">John Hay Library</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Brown_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: John Hay Library">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <div class="rellink relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/John_Hay_Library" title="John Hay Library">John Hay Library</a>
     </div> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:BrownUniversity-JohnHayLibrary.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8f/BrownUniversity-JohnHayLibrary.jpg/220px-BrownUniversity-JohnHayLibrary.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8f/BrownUniversity-JohnHayLibrary.jpg/330px-BrownUniversity-JohnHayLibrary.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8f/BrownUniversity-JohnHayLibrary.jpg/440px-BrownUniversity-JohnHayLibrary.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:BrownUniversity-JohnHayLibrary.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf8/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> The 
        <a href="/wiki/John_Hay_Library" title="John Hay Library">John Hay Library</a>
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>The John Hay Library is the second oldest library on campus. It was named for <a href="/wiki/John_Hay" title="John Hay">John Hay</a> (class of 1858, private secretary to <a href="/wiki/Abraham_Lincoln" title="Abraham Lincoln">Abraham Lincoln</a> and Secretary of State under two Presidents) at the request of his friend <a href="/wiki/Andrew_Carnegie" title="Andrew Carnegie">Andrew Carnegie</a>, who contributed half of the $300,000 cost of the building.<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93"><span>[</span>93<span>]</span></a></sup> Constructed with <a href="/wiki/Vermont" title="Vermont">Vermont</a> white <a href="/wiki/Marble" title="Marble">marble</a> in an <a href="/wiki/English_Renaissance" title="English Renaissance">English Renaissance</a> style, the library was dedicated on 10 November 1910 and had an estimated collection of 300,000 volumes.<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94"><span>[</span>94<span>]</span></a></sup> It is now the repository of Brown University archives, rare books and manuscripts, and special collections. Noteworthy among the latter are the <a href="/wiki/Anne_S._K._Brown_Military_Collection" title="Anne S. K. Brown Military Collection">Anne S. K. Brown Military Collection</a><sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95"><span>[</span>95<span>]</span></a></sup> (described as &quot;the foremost American collection of material devoted to the history and iconography of soldiers and soldiering&quot;), the Harris Collection of American Poetry and Plays (described as &quot;the largest and most comprehensive collection of its kind in any research library&quot;), the Lownes Collection of the History of Science (described as &quot;one of the three most important private collections of books of science in America&quot;), and (for popularity of requests) the papers of <a href="/wiki/H.P._Lovecraft" title="H.P. Lovecraft" class="mw-redirect">H.P. Lovecraft</a>. The Hay Library is home to one of the broadest collections of <a href="/wiki/Incunable" title="Incunable">incunabula</a> (15th-century printed books) in the Americas, as well as such rarities as the manuscript of <a href="/wiki/George_Orwell" title="George Orwell">Orwell</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/Nineteen_Eighty-Four" title="Nineteen Eighty-Four">Nineteen Eighty-Four</a></i> and a Shakespeare <a href="/wiki/First_Folio" title="First Folio">First Folio</a>. There are also three books <a href="/wiki/Anthropodermic_bibliopegy" title="Anthropodermic bibliopegy">bound in human skin</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96"><span>[</span>96<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The <a href="/wiki/Pembroke_Center_for_Teaching_and_Research_on_Women" title="Pembroke Center for Teaching and Research on Women">Pembroke Center for Teaching and Research on Women</a> manages the Elizabeth Weed Feminist Theory Papers and the Christine Dunlap Farnham Archives, both rich resources for feminist scholars.</p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="John_Carter_Brown_Library">John Carter Brown Library</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Brown_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: John Carter Brown Library">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <div class="thumb tleft"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Brown_university_john_carter_brown_lib.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/Brown_university_john_carter_brown_lib.JPG/220px-Brown_university_john_carter_brown_lib.JPG" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/Brown_university_john_carter_brown_lib.JPG/330px-Brown_university_john_carter_brown_lib.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/Brown_university_john_carter_brown_lib.JPG/440px-Brown_university_john_carter_brown_lib.JPG 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Brown_university_john_carter_brown_lib.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf8/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> The 
        <a href="/wiki/John_Carter_Brown_Library" title="John Carter Brown Library">John Carter Brown Library</a>
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <div class="rellink relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/John_Carter_Brown_Library" title="John Carter Brown Library">John Carter Brown Library</a>
     </div> 
     <p>The John Carter Brown Library, founded in 1846, is administered separately from the University, but has been located on the Main Green of the campus since 1904. It is generally regarded as the world's leading collection of primary historical sources pertaining to the Americas before 1825. It houses a very large percentage of the titles published before that date about the discovery, settlement, history, and natural history of the New World. The &quot;JCB&quot;, as it is known, publishes <i>Bibliotheca Americana</i>, the main bibliography in the field. Typical of its noteworthy holdings is the best preserved of the seven surviving copies of <a href="/wiki/Bay_Psalm_Book" title="Bay Psalm Book">Bay Psalm Book</a>, the first extant book printed in British North America. There is also a very fine Shakespeare <a href="/wiki/First_Folio" title="First Folio">First Folio</a>, added to the collection by John Carter Brown's widow (a Shakespeare enthusiast) on the grounds that it includes <i><a href="/wiki/The_Tempest" title="The Tempest">The Tempest</a></i>, a play set in the New World. The JCB holdings comprise more than 50,000 early titles and about 16,000 modern books, as well as prints, manuscripts, maps, and other items in the library's specialty. The JCB occupies a <a href="/wiki/Beaux-Arts_architecture" title="Beaux-Arts architecture">Beaux-Arts</a> style building designed by <a href="/wiki/Shepley,_Rutan,_and_Coolidge" title="Shepley, Rutan, and Coolidge" class="mw-redirect">Shepley, Rutan, and Coolidge</a>. The 1904 edifice was expanded in 1990 by architects Hartman-Cox of Washington, D.C.</p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Haffenreffer_Museum_of_Anthropology">Haffenreffer Museum of Anthropology</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Brown_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Haffenreffer Museum of Anthropology">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <div class="rellink relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/Haffenreffer_Museum_of_Anthropology" title="Haffenreffer Museum of Anthropology">Haffenreffer Museum of Anthropology</a>
     </div> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Haffenreffer_Museum_of_Anthropology,_Providence_RI.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d0/Haffenreffer_Museum_of_Anthropology%2C_Providence_RI.jpg/220px-Haffenreffer_Museum_of_Anthropology%2C_Providence_RI.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d0/Haffenreffer_Museum_of_Anthropology%2C_Providence_RI.jpg/330px-Haffenreffer_Museum_of_Anthropology%2C_Providence_RI.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d0/Haffenreffer_Museum_of_Anthropology%2C_Providence_RI.jpg/440px-Haffenreffer_Museum_of_Anthropology%2C_Providence_RI.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Haffenreffer_Museum_of_Anthropology,_Providence_RI.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf8/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> Manning Hall, Home to the 
        <a href="/wiki/Haffenreffer_Museum_of_Anthropology" title="Haffenreffer Museum of Anthropology">Haffenreffer Museum of Anthropology</a>
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>The exhibition galleries of the Haffenreffer Museum of Anthropology, Brown's teaching museum, are located in Manning Hall on the campus's main green. Its one million artifacts, available for research and educational purposes, are located at its Collections Research Center in Bristol, RI. The museum's goal is to inspire creative and critical thinking about culture by fostering interdisciplinary understanding of the material world. It provides opportunities for faculty and students to work with collections and the public, teaching through objects and programs in classrooms and exhibitions. The museum sponsors lectures and events in all areas of anthropology, and also runs an extensive program of outreach to local schools.</p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sustainability">Sustainability</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Brown_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Sustainability">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>Brown University has committed to &quot;minimize its energy use, reduce negative environmental impacts and promote environmental stewardship.&quot;<sup id="cite_ref-Brown.27s_Energy_and_Environmental_Mission_97-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Brown.27s_Energy_and_Environmental_Mission-97"><span>[</span>97<span>]</span></a></sup> The Energy and Environmental Advisory Committee has developed a set of ambitious goals for the university to reduce its <a href="/wiki/Carbon_emissions" title="Carbon emissions" class="mw-redirect">carbon emissions</a> and eventually achieve <a href="/wiki/Carbon_neutrality" title="Carbon neutrality">carbon neutrality</a>. The Brown is Green website collects information about Brown's progress toward greenhouse gas emissions reductions and related campus initiatives like courses, research, projects and student groups.<sup id="cite_ref-Brown_is_Green_98-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Brown_is_Green-98"><span>[</span>98<span>]</span></a></sup> Brown received an A- on the 2009 College Sustainability Report Card, developed by the Sustainable Endowments Institute. Brown was one of only 15 schools to receive a grade above a B+. There were no schools in the report that received an &quot;A&quot;.<sup id="cite_ref-Sustainable_Endowments_Institute_Report_Card_99-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sustainable_Endowments_Institute_Report_Card-99"><span>[</span>99<span>]</span></a></sup> Brown has a number of active environmental leadership groups on campus.<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100"><span>[</span>100<span>]</span></a></sup> These groups have begun a number of campus-wide environmental initiatives?including promoting the reduction of supply and demand of bottled water and investigating a composting program.</p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Boldly_Brown">Boldly Brown</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Brown_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Boldly Brown">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>Under President Ruth Simmons, the University has launched Boldly Brown: The Campaign for Academic Enrichment. This campaign consists of re-evaluating the existing curriculum and raising money for greater academic ambition. The money will be used for academic programs, research, new facilities, biology and medicine, students who need financial assistance, and expanding the faculty and staff. In June 2009, it was announced that the campaign had met its goal 19 months ahead of target, with record levels of giving despite the global economic crises of the fiscal year. The total sum raised currently stands at over US$1.5 billion.<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101"><span>[</span>101<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Student_life">Student life</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Brown_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Student life">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Atmosphere">Atmosphere</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Brown_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Atmosphere">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>Brown University has recently been ranked #1 for America's Happiest College Students, according to the Princeton Review 2010 rankings.<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102"><span>[</span>102<span>]</span></a></sup> Brown was also named &quot;the most fashionable school in the Ivy League&quot; by the <a href="/wiki/Fashion" title="Fashion">fashion</a> trade journal <i><a href="/wiki/Women%27s_Wear_Daily" title="Women's Wear Daily">Women's Wear Daily</a></i> on the basis that students on campus seem to have the strongest sense of personal style.<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103"><span>[</span>103<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Athletics">Athletics</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Brown_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Athletics">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <div class="rellink relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/Brown_Bears" title="Brown Bears">Brown Bears</a>
     </div> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Harvard_crimsons_v_brown_2009.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/Harvard_crimsons_v_brown_2009.JPG/220px-Harvard_crimsons_v_brown_2009.JPG" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/Harvard_crimsons_v_brown_2009.JPG/330px-Harvard_crimsons_v_brown_2009.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/Harvard_crimsons_v_brown_2009.JPG/440px-Harvard_crimsons_v_brown_2009.JPG 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Harvard_crimsons_v_brown_2009.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf8/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> Brown vs. 
        <a href="/wiki/Harvard_University" title="Harvard University">Harvard</a>, September 2009
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>Brown is a member of the <a href="/wiki/National_Collegiate_Athletic_Association" title="National Collegiate Athletic Association">National Collegiate Athletic Association</a> (NCAA) <a href="/wiki/Division_I_(NCAA)" title="Division I (NCAA)">Division I</a> <a href="/wiki/Ivy_League" title="Ivy League">Ivy League</a> athletic conference. It sponsors 37 <a href="/wiki/Varsity_team" title="Varsity team">varsity</a> intercollegiate teams. Its athletic programs have been featured in the College Sports Honor Roll as one of the top 20 athletic programs in the country according to U.S. News &amp; World Report. Brown Women's Rowing Team has won 6 national titles in the last 12 years, the Men's Rowing Team perennially finishes in the top 5 in the nation and swept the <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Sprints" title="Eastern Sprints">Eastern Sprints</a> in 2009. Brown Football's reemergence, and its surge in northeast college popularity generally, is credited to its historic 1976 Ivy League championship team, which was Brown's first Ivy League Football Champions. The 1976 &quot;Magnificent Andersons,&quot; so named for its coach, John Anderson, was 8?1, tying it with Yale, which the 1976 Brown team defeated head to head that year, and included an ABC Sports televised football game, defeating Harvard 16?14. Since the 1976 football championship season, Brown Football has won three Ivy League championships under the most successful coach in its history, Phil Estes: 1999, 2005, and 2008. Brown's Men's Soccer program is consistently ranked in the top 25 and has won 18 Ivy League titles overall, including 8 of the last 12. Recent graduates play professionally in Major League Soccer and overseas. The Men's Lacrosse team also has a long and storied history, and more recently the program has again attained national rankings and exposure. In 2007, Brown won its first Ivy League baseball championship in school history. Brown's Varsity Equestrian team won the Ivy League Championships for the past two years in a row, and has consistently performed extremely well within the team's zone and region.<sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104"><span>[</span>104<span>]</span></a></sup> Brown also features several competitive intercollegiate club sports, including <a href="/wiki/Sailing" title="Sailing">Sailing</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ultimate_(sport)" title="Ultimate (sport)">Ultimate</a>, and Women's Rugby teams. In 2005, the Men's Club Ultimate Frisbee team, <a href="/wiki/Brownian_Motion_(Ultimate)" title="Brownian Motion (Ultimate)" class="mw-redirect">Brownian Motion</a>, won the National Championships.</p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Student_organizations">Student organizations</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Brown_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Student organizations">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <div class="rellink boilerplate seealso">
      See also: 
      <a href="/wiki/Category:Brown_University_organizations" title="Category:Brown University organizations">Category:Brown University organizations</a>
     </div> 
     <p>There are over 300 registered student organizations on campus with diverse interests. The Student Activities Fair, during the orientation program, provides first-year students the opportunity to become acquainted with the wide range of organizations.</p>

     <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Residential_and_Greek_Societies">Residential and Greek Societies</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Brown_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: Residential and Greek Societies">edit</a>]</span></h4> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:BrownUniversity-MarcyHouse.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/BrownUniversity-MarcyHouse.jpg/170px-BrownUniversity-MarcyHouse.jpg" width="170" height="227" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/BrownUniversity-MarcyHouse.jpg/255px-BrownUniversity-MarcyHouse.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/BrownUniversity-MarcyHouse.jpg/340px-BrownUniversity-MarcyHouse.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:BrownUniversity-MarcyHouse.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf8/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> A fraternity house in Wriston Quadrangle
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>12.7% of Brown students are in <a href="/wiki/Fraternities_and_sororities" title="Fraternities and sororities" class="mw-redirect">fraternities or sororities</a>. There are 10 residential Greek houses: six all-male fraternities (<a href="/wiki/Alpha_Epsilon_Pi" title="Alpha Epsilon Pi">Alpha Epsilon Pi</a>, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Delta_Tau&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Delta Tau (page does not exist)">Delta Tau</a>, <a href="/wiki/Delta_Phi" title="Delta Phi">Delta Phi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Theta_Delta_Chi" title="Theta Delta Chi">Theta Delta Chi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sigma_Chi" title="Sigma Chi">Sigma Chi</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Phi_Kappa_Psi" title="Phi Kappa Psi">Phi Kappa Psi</a>), three sororities (<a href="/wiki/Alpha_Chi_Omega" title="Alpha Chi Omega">Alpha Chi Omega</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kappa_Alpha_Theta" title="Kappa Alpha Theta">Kappa Alpha Theta</a>), and, as of March 2013, <a href="/wiki/Kappa_Delta" title="Kappa Delta">Kappa Delta</a>), one co-ed fraternity (Zeta Delta Xi), and one co-ed literary society (<a href="/wiki/Alpha_Delta_Phi#The_Society" title="Alpha Delta Phi">Alpha Delta Phi</a>). All recognized Greek letter organizations live on-campus in University-owned dorm housing. All ten Greek houses are overseen by the Greek Council and are located on Wriston Quadrangle.</p> 
     <p>An alternative to fraternity life at Brown are the program houses, which are organized around various themes. As with Greek houses, the existing residents of each house take applications from students, usually at the start of the Spring semester. Examples of program houses include: <a href="/wiki/St._Anthony_Hall" title="St. Anthony Hall">St. Anthony Hall</a> (located in King House), Buxton International House, the Machado <a href="/wiki/French_language" title="French language">French</a>/<a href="/wiki/Hispanic" title="Hispanic">Hispanic</a> House, Technology House, Harambee (African culture) House, Culinary Arts (Cooking) House and <a href="/wiki/Interfaith" title="Interfaith" class="mw-redirect">Interfaith</a> House.</p> 
     <p>Currently, there are three student cooperative houses at Brown. Two of the houses, Watermyn and Finlandia on Waterman Street, are owned by the <a href="/wiki/Brown_Association_for_Cooperative_Housing" title="Brown Association for Cooperative Housing">Brown Association for Cooperative Housing</a> (BACH), an independent non-profit corporation owned and operated by house members.</p> 
     <p>The third co-op, West House, is located in a Brown-owned house on Brown Street. All three houses also run a vegetarian food co-op for residents and non-residents.</p> 
     <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Secret_Societies">Secret Societies</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Brown_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: Secret Societies">edit</a>]</span></h4> 
     <p>Secret societies at Brown originated as literary clubs in the mid-18th century, and primarily existed to organize debates among their members. One early literary club was the Pronouncing Society, which disbanded in the mid-1770s.<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106"><span>[</span>106<span>]</span></a></sup> Another was Athenian at Queen's, founded in 1776 but also dissolved shortly afterwards.<sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107"><span>[</span>107<span>]</span></a></sup> The Philermenian Society (founded as the Misokosmian Society) arose in 1794.<sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108"><span>[</span>108<span>]</span></a></sup> In reaction to the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Federalist_Party" title="United States Federalist Party" class="mw-redirect">Federalist</a> Philermenians, a <a href="/wiki/United_States_Democratic-Republican_Party" title="United States Democratic-Republican Party" class="mw-redirect">Democratic-Republican</a> club called the United Brothers Society organized in 1806.<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109"><span>[</span>109<span>]</span></a></sup> In 1824 a third group, the <a href="/wiki/Franklin_Society" title="Franklin Society" class="mw-redirect">Franklin Society</a>, was formally recognized by the university president, and counted as honorary members <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Jefferson" title="Thomas Jefferson">Thomas Jefferson</a>, <a href="/wiki/John_Quincy_Adams" title="John Quincy Adams">John Quincy Adams</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Henry_Clay" title="Henry Clay">Henry Clay</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110"><span>[</span>110<span>]</span></a></sup> However, by the Civil War, most of these organizations had dissipated on account of newer Greek letter <a href="/wiki/Fraternities_and_sororities" title="Fraternities and sororities" class="mw-redirect">fraternities</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111"><span>[</span>111<span>]</span></a></sup> There remains some dispute over the presence of these groups today, and at least one student organization, Pacifica House, claims descent from early secret societies.<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112"><span>[</span>112<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113"><span>[</span>113<span>]</span></a></sup> The Undergraduate Council of Students, Brown's student government, also reflects this historical legacy. The UCS originated as the Cammarian Club in 1893, a semi-secret senior society that served as an intermediary between the student body and the administration, and which ritualistically &quot;tapped&quot; 15 new men each year until its dissolution after World War II.<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114"><span>[</span>114<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Traditions">Traditions</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Brown_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: Traditions">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <div class="rellink relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/Brown_University_traditions" title="Brown University traditions">Brown University traditions</a>
     </div> 
     <p>Though the early history of Brown as a men's school includes a number of unusual <a href="/wiki/Hazing" title="Hazing">hazing</a> traditions, the University's present-day traditions tend to be non-violent while maintaining the spirit of zaniness.<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115"><span>[</span>115<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Van_Wickle_Gates">Van Wickle Gates</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Brown_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=40" title="Edit section: Van Wickle Gates">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:ScannedImage-11.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/0/0f/ScannedImage-11.JPG/220px-ScannedImage-11.JPG" width="220" height="140" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/0/0f/ScannedImage-11.JPG/330px-ScannedImage-11.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/0/0f/ScannedImage-11.JPG/440px-ScannedImage-11.JPG 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:ScannedImage-11.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf8/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> Front view of the 
        <a href="/wiki/Van_Wickle_Gates" title="Van Wickle Gates">Van Wickle Gates</a>
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <div class="rellink relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/Van_Wickle_Gates" title="Van Wickle Gates">Van Wickle Gates</a>
     </div> 
     <p>The Van Wickle Gates, dedicated on 18 June 1901, have a pair of center gates and a smaller gate on each side. The side gates remain open throughout the year, while the center gates remain closed except for two occasions each year. At the beginning of the academic year, the center gates open inward to admit students during Convocation. At the end of the second semester, the gates open outward for the Commencement Day procession.<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116"><span>[</span>116<span>]</span></a></sup> A traditional superstition is that students who pass through the gates for a second time before graduation do not graduate. The <a href="/wiki/Brown_University_Band" title="Brown University Band">Brown University Band</a> famously flouts this tradition by marching in the yearly commencement procession. Undergraduate members, however, walk through the gates backwards, thereby avoiding the hex.</p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Josiah_S._Carberry">Josiah S. Carberry</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Brown_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=41" title="Edit section: Josiah S. Carberry">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <div class="rellink relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/Josiah_S._Carberry" title="Josiah S. Carberry">Josiah S. Carberry</a>
     </div> 
     <p>One of Brown's most notable traditions is keeping alive the spirit and accomplishments of <a href="/wiki/Josiah_S._Carberry" title="Josiah S. Carberry">Josiah S. Carberry</a>, the fictional Professor of Psychoceramics (the equally fictional study of <a href="/wiki/Crank_(person)" title="Crank (person)">cracked pots</a>), who was born on a University Hall billboard in 1929. He is the namesake of &quot;Josiah's&quot;, a University-run campus eatery. &quot;Josiah&quot; is also the name of the University's electronic library catalog.</p> 
     <p>According to Martha Mitchell's <i><a href="/wiki/Encyclopedia_Brunoniana" title="Encyclopedia Brunoniana">Encyclopedia Brunoniana</a></i>, &quot;On Friday, May 13, 1955, an anonymous gift of $101.01 was received by the University from Professor Carberry to establish the Josiah S. Carberry Fund in memory of his 'future late wife.' A condition of the gift was that, henceforth, every Friday the 13th would be designated 'Carberry Day,' and on that day friends of the University would deposit their loose change in brown jugs to augment the fund, which is used to purchase 'such books as Professor Carberry might or might not approve of.'&quot;<sup id="cite_ref-EB_117-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EB-117"><span>[</span>117<span>]</span></a></sup> Students have followed this tradition ever since, and the fund currently has over $10,000 in it.<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118"><span>[</span>118<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>Mitchell writes, &quot;Professor Carberry has been the subject of articles in a number of periodicals, including <i>The New York Times</i>, which proclaimed him 'The World's Greatest Traveler' on the front page of its Sunday travel section in 1974, and in <i>Yankee</i> magazine, where he was 'The Absent-Bodied Professor' in 1975. A recent honor which came to Professor Carberry was the award to him of an <a href="/wiki/Ig_Nobel_Prize" title="Ig Nobel Prize">Ig Nobel Prize</a> at the First Annual Ig Nobel Prize Ceremony in 1991. At this event sponsored by <a href="/wiki/Massachusetts_Institute_of_Technology" title="Massachusetts Institute of Technology">M.I.T.</a> and the <i><a href="/wiki/Journal_of_Irreproducible_Results" title="Journal of Irreproducible Results">Journal of Irreproducible Results</a></i>, Carberry, the 1991 Ig Nobel Interdisciplinary Research Prize laureate, was cited as 'bold explorer and eclectic seeker of knowledge, for his pioneering work in the field of psychoceramics, the study of cracked pots.'&quot;<sup id="cite_ref-EB_117-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EB-117"><span>[</span>117<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Spring_Weekend">Spring Weekend</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Brown_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=42" title="Edit section: Spring Weekend">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <div class="rellink relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/Brown_University_traditions#Spring_Weekend" title="Brown University traditions">Spring Weekend</a>
     </div> 
     <p>Starting in 1950, Brown replaced the traditional Junior Week and Junior Prom, which were discontinued during World War II, with Spring Weekend, which featured athletic contests and dances. Concerts featuring invited performers began in 1960, including <a href="/wiki/Bob_Dylan" title="Bob Dylan">Bob Dylan</a>, <a href="/wiki/U2" title="U2">U2</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bruce_Springsteen" title="Bruce Springsteen">Bruce Springsteen</a>, <a href="/wiki/Janis_Joplin" title="Janis Joplin">Janis Joplin</a>, <a href="/wiki/James_Brown" title="James Brown">James Brown</a> and <a href="/wiki/Snoop_Dogg" title="Snoop Dogg">Snoop Dogg</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119"><span>[</span>119<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120"><span>[</span>120<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Alma_Mater">Alma Mater</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Brown_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=43" title="Edit section: Alma Mater">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <div class="rellink relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/Brown_University_Alma_Mater" title="Brown University Alma Mater">Brown University Alma Mater</a>
     </div> 
     <p>The &quot;Alma Mater&quot; was written by James Andrews DeWolf (Class of 1861) in 1860, who named it &quot;Old Brown&quot; and set it to the tune of &quot;<a href="/wiki/1822_in_music" title="1822 in music">Araby's Daughter</a>&quot; (which was later known as &quot;<a href="/wiki/Samuel_Woodworth" title="Samuel Woodworth">The Old Oaken Bucket</a>&quot;). The song was renamed &quot;Alma Mater&quot;, after the <a href="/wiki/Incipit" title="Incipit">incipit</a>, in 1869.<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121"><span>[</span>121<span>]</span></a></sup> It is sung and played after varsity athletic victories and at formal events such as Convocation and Commencement.</p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notable_alumni_and_faculty">Notable alumni and faculty</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Brown_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=44" title="Edit section: Notable alumni and faculty">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <div class="rellink relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/List_of_Brown_University_people" title="List of Brown University people">List of Brown University people</a>
     </div>

     <p>Chief Justice of the U.S. Supreme Court and Secretary of State <a href="/wiki/Charles_Evans_Hughes" title="Charles Evans Hughes">Charles Evans Hughes</a> (1881), father of American public school education <a href="/wiki/Horace_Mann" title="Horace Mann">Horace Mann</a> (1819), philanthropist <a href="/wiki/John_D._Rockefeller_Jr." title="John D. Rockefeller Jr." class="mw-redirect">John D. Rockefeller Jr.</a> (1897), Secretary of State <a href="/wiki/John_Hay" title="John Hay">John Hay</a> (1852), philosopher, civil <a href="/wiki/Libertarianism" title="Libertarianism">libertarian</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Amherst_College" title="Amherst College">Amherst College</a> president <a href="/wiki/Alexander_Meiklejohn" title="Alexander Meiklejohn">Alexander Meiklejohn</a>, first president of the <a href="/wiki/University_of_South_Carolina" title="University of South Carolina">University of South Carolina</a> <a href="/wiki/Jonathan_Maxcy" title="Jonathan Maxcy">Jonathan Maxcy</a> (1787), <a href="/wiki/Bates_College" title="Bates College">Bates College</a> founder <a href="/wiki/Oren_B._Cheney" title="Oren B. Cheney">Oren B. Cheney</a> (1836), <a href="/wiki/Governor_of_Wyoming" title="Governor of Wyoming" class="mw-redirect">Governor of Wyoming Territory</a> and <a href="/wiki/Governor_of_Nebraska" title="Governor of Nebraska">Governor of Nebraska</a> <a href="/wiki/John_Milton_Thayer" title="John Milton Thayer">John Milton Thayer</a> (1841), longest-serving <a href="/wiki/University_of_Michigan" title="University of Michigan">University of Michigan</a> president (1871?1909) <a href="/wiki/James_Burrill_Angell" title="James Burrill Angell">James Burrill Angell</a> (1849), notable <a href="/wiki/University_of_California" title="University of California">University of California</a> president (1899?1919) <a href="/wiki/Benjamin_Ide_Wheeler" title="Benjamin Ide Wheeler">Benjamin Ide Wheeler</a> (1875), <a href="/wiki/Morehouse_College" title="Morehouse College">Morehouse College</a>'s first African-American president <a href="/wiki/John_Hope_(educator)" title="John Hope (educator)">John Hope</a> (1894), magazine editor <a href="/wiki/John_F._Kennedy,_Jr." title="John F. Kennedy, Jr.">John F. Kennedy, Jr.</a> '83, diplomat <a href="/wiki/Richard_Holbrooke" title="Richard Holbrooke">Richard Holbrooke</a> '62, <a href="/wiki/World_Bank" title="World Bank">World Bank</a> president and former <a href="/wiki/Dartmouth_College" title="Dartmouth College">Dartmouth College</a> president <a href="/wiki/Jim_Yong_Kim" title="Jim Yong Kim">Jim Yong Kim</a> '82, <a href="/wiki/NASA" title="NASA">NASA</a> head during first seven <a href="/wiki/Apollo_program" title="Apollo program">Apollo</a> missions <a href="/wiki/Thomas_O._Paine" title="Thomas O. Paine">Thomas O. Paine</a> '42, chief scientist <a href="/wiki/NASA" title="NASA">NASA</a> Mars and lunar programs James B. Garvin '78.</p> 
     <p>Alumni who are currently governors of states are <a href="/wiki/Bobby_Jindal" title="Bobby Jindal">Bobby Jindal</a> '91 of Louisiana, <a href="/wiki/Maggie_Hassan" title="Maggie Hassan">Maggie Hassan</a> '80 of New Hampshire, <a href="/wiki/Jack_Markell" title="Jack Markell">Jack Markell</a> '82 of Delaware, and <a href="/wiki/Lincoln_Chafee" title="Lincoln Chafee">Lincoln Chafee</a> '75 of Rhode Island.</p> 
     <p>Business and finance figures include <a href="/wiki/IBM" title="IBM">IBM</a> chair and CEO <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Watson,_Jr." title="Thomas Watson, Jr.">Thomas Watson, Jr.</a> '37, <a href="/wiki/CNN" title="CNN">CNN</a> founder and <a href="/wiki/America%27s_Cup" title="America's Cup">America's Cup</a> yachtsman <a href="/wiki/Ted_Turner" title="Ted Turner">Ted Turner</a> '60, <a href="/wiki/Bank_of_America" title="Bank of America">Bank of America</a> CEO <a href="/wiki/Brian_Moynihan" title="Brian Moynihan">Brian Moynihan</a> '81, financial analyst <a href="/wiki/Meredith_Whitney" title="Meredith Whitney">Meredith Whitney</a>, <a href="/wiki/McKinsey_%26_Co." title="McKinsey &amp; Co." class="mw-redirect">McKinsey &amp; Co.</a> co-founder and father of modern management consulting <a href="/wiki/Marvin_Bower" title="Marvin Bower">Marvin Bower</a> '25, <a href="/wiki/Group_of_Thirty" title="Group of Thirty">Group of Thirty</a> member and <a href="/wiki/Citibank" title="Citibank">Citibank</a> chairman <a href="/wiki/William_R._Rhodes" title="William R. Rhodes">William R. Rhodes</a> '57, <a href="/wiki/Chase_(bank)" title="Chase (bank)">Chase Bank</a> chairman and CEO <a href="/wiki/Willard_C._Butcher" title="Willard C. Butcher">Willard C. Butcher</a> '48, <a href="/wiki/Tiffany_%26_Co" title="Tiffany &amp; Co" class="mw-redirect">Tiffany &amp; Co</a> CEO Walter Hoving '20, <a href="/wiki/Motorola" title="Motorola">Motorola</a> and <a href="/wiki/Eastman_Kodak" title="Eastman Kodak">Eastman Kodak</a> chairman and CEO <a href="/wiki/George_M._C._Fisher" title="George M. C. Fisher">George M. C. Fisher</a> (ScM '64, PhD '66), <a href="/wiki/NASDAQ" title="NASDAQ">NASDAQ</a> first president and CEO <a href="/wiki/Gordon_Macklin" title="Gordon Macklin">Gordon Macklin</a> '50, <a href="/wiki/Quadrangle_Group" title="Quadrangle Group">Quadrangle Group</a> founder and <a href="/wiki/US_Treasury_Department" title="US Treasury Department" class="mw-redirect">Treasury Department</a> &quot;Car Czar&quot; for auto industry reorganization <a href="/wiki/Steven_Rattner" title="Steven Rattner">Steven Rattner</a> '74, former Securities and Exchange Commissioner, Annette Nazareth '78.</p> 
     <p>Alumni in the computer sciences and industry include <a href="/wiki/Apple_Macintosh" title="Apple Macintosh" class="mw-redirect">Apple Macintosh</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mac_OS" title="Mac OS">Mac OS</a> designer <a href="/wiki/Andy_Hertzfeld" title="Andy Hertzfeld">Andy Hertzfeld</a> '75, architect of <a href="/wiki/Intel_80386" title="Intel 80386">Intel 386</a>, <a href="/wiki/Intel_80486" title="Intel 80486">486</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Pentium" title="Pentium">Pentium</a> microprocessors <a href="/wiki/John_H._Crawford" title="John H. Crawford" class="mw-redirect">John H. Crawford</a> '75, first <a href="/wiki/Microsoft" title="Microsoft">Microsoft</a> <a href="/wiki/Microsoft_Windows" title="Microsoft Windows">Windows</a> project chief <a href="/wiki/Brad_Silverberg" title="Brad Silverberg">Brad Silverberg</a>, <a href="/wiki/Apple_Computer" title="Apple Computer" class="mw-redirect">Apple Computer</a> CEO (1983?1993) <a href="/wiki/John_Sculley" title="John Sculley">John Sculley</a> '61, <a href="/wiki/Massachusetts_Institute_of_Technology" title="Massachusetts Institute of Technology">MIT</a> computer science chair <a href="/wiki/John_Guttag" title="John Guttag">John Guttag</a> '71, <a href="/wiki/University_of_Washington" title="University of Washington">University of Washington</a> computer science chair <a href="/wiki/Edward_D._Lazowska" title="Edward D. Lazowska">Ed Lazowska</a> '72, inventor of the first silicon transistor <a href="/wiki/Gordon_Kidd_Teal" title="Gordon Kidd Teal">Gordon Kidd Teal</a> '31.</p>

     <p>Alumni in the arts and media include actress <a href="/wiki/Laura_Linney" title="Laura Linney">Laura Linney</a> '86, actor <a href="/wiki/John_Krasinski" title="John Krasinski">John Krasinski</a> '01, <a href="/wiki/Modern_Family" title="Modern Family">Modern Family</a> actress <a href="/wiki/Julie_Bowen" title="Julie Bowen">Julie Bowen</a> '91, <a href="/wiki/Harry_Potter_(film_series)" title="Harry Potter (film series)"><i>Harry Potter</i> films</a> actress <a href="/wiki/Emma_Watson" title="Emma Watson">Emma Watson</a> '13, MSNBC program hosts <a href="/wiki/Chris_Hayes_(journalist)" title="Chris Hayes (journalist)">Chris Hayes</a> '01 and <a href="/wiki/Alex_Wagner" title="Alex Wagner">Alex Wagner</a> '99, NPR program host <a href="/wiki/Ira_Glass" title="Ira Glass">Ira Glass</a> '82, singer-composer <a href="/wiki/Mary_Chapin_Carpenter" title="Mary Chapin Carpenter">Mary Chapin Carpenter</a> '81, <i><a href="/wiki/CSI:_NY" title="CSI: NY">CSI: NY</a></i> actor <a href="/wiki/Hill_Harper" title="Hill Harper">Hill Harper</a>, musicians <a href="/wiki/Damian_Kulash" title="Damian Kulash">Damian Kulash</a> '98 and <a href="/wiki/Dhani_Harrison" title="Dhani Harrison">Dhani Harrison</a> '02, film directors <a href="/wiki/Todd_Haynes" title="Todd Haynes">Todd Haynes</a> '85, <a href="/wiki/Doug_Liman" title="Doug Liman">Doug Liman</a> '88, and <a href="/wiki/Davis_Guggenheim" title="Davis Guggenheim">Davis Guggenheim</a> '86, and director-actor <a href="/wiki/Tim_Blake_Nelson" title="Tim Blake Nelson">Tim Blake Nelson</a> '86, <i><a href="/wiki/The_New_Yorker" title="The New Yorker">New Yorker</a></i> humorist and <a href="/wiki/Marx_Brothers" title="Marx Brothers">Marx Brothers</a> screenwriter <a href="/wiki/S.J._Perelman" title="S.J.      <p>Other notable alumni include <a href="/wiki/Pro_Football_Hall_of_Fame" title="Pro Football Hall of Fame">Pro Football Hall of Fame</a> sportscaster <a href="/wiki/Chris_Berman" title="Chris Berman">Chris Berman</a> '77, <a href="/wiki/Pennsylvania_State_University" title="Pennsylvania State University">Penn State</a> football coach <a href="/wiki/Joe_Paterno" title="Joe Paterno">Joe Paterno</a> '50, <a href="/wiki/Heisman_Trophy" title="Heisman Trophy">Heisman Trophy</a> namesake <a href="/wiki/John_W._Heisman" title="John W. Heisman" class="mw-redirect">John W. Heisman</a> '91, Pollard Award namesake and first black All-American and NFL head coach <a href="/wiki/Fritz_Pollard" title="Fritz Pollard">Fritz Pollard</a> '19, <a href="/wiki/National_Security_Council" title="National Security Council">National Security Council</a> counter-terrorism director <a href="/wiki/RP_Eddy" title="RP Eddy" class="mw-redirect">RP Eddy</a> '94, presidential advisor <a href="/wiki/Ira_Magaziner" title="Ira Magaziner">Ira Magaziner</a> '69, founder of The Gratitude Network and The Intersection event <a href="/wiki/Randy_Haykin" title="Randy Haykin">Randy Haykin</a> '85. Also <a href="/wiki/Royalty" title="Royalty">royals</a> and <a href="/wiki/Nobility" title="Nobility">nobles</a> such as <a href="/wiki/Prince_Rahim_Aga_Khan" title="Prince Rahim Aga Khan" class="mw-redirect">Prince Rahim Aga Khan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Prince_Faisal_bin_Al_Hussein" title="Prince Faisal bin Al Hussein" class="mw-redirect">Prince Faisal bin Al Hussein</a>, <a href="/wiki/Prince_Nikolaos_of_Greece_and_Denmark" title="Prince Nikolaos of Greece and Denmark">Prince Nikolaos of Greece and Denmark</a>, <a href="/wiki/Prince_Nikita_Romanov" title="Prince Nikita Romanov">Prince Nikita Romanov</a>, <a href="/wiki/Princess_Theodora_of_Greece_and_Denmark" title="Princess Theodora of Greece and Denmark">Princess Theodora of Greece and Denmark</a>, <a href="/wiki/Prince_Jaime,_Count_of_Bardi" title="Prince Jaime, Count of Bardi">Prince Jaime of Bourbon-Parma, Duke of San Jaime and Count of Bardi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Prince_Ra%27ad_bin_Zeid" title="Prince Ra'ad bin Zeid" class="mw-redirect">Prince Ra'ad bin Zeid</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lady_Gabriella_Windsor" title="Lady Gabriella Windsor">Lady Gabriella Windsor</a>, <a href="/wiki/Alexander_von_F%C3%BCrstenberg" title="Alexander von F&uuml;rstenberg">Prince Alexander von F&uuml;rstenberg</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cosima_von_B%C3%BClow_Pavoncelli" title="Cosima von B&uuml;low Pavoncelli">Countess Cosima von B&uuml;low Pavoncelli</a>.</p> 
     <p><a href="/wiki/New_York_Institute_of_Technology" title="New York Institute of Technology">New York Institute of Technology</a> president Edward Guiliano, <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Prize" title="Nobel Prize">Nobel</a> Laureates <a href="/wiki/Craig_Mello" title="Craig Mello">Craig Mello</a> '82 and <a href="/wiki/Jerry_White_(activist)" title="Jerry White (activist)">Jerry White</a> '87, <a href="/wiki/Cooley-Tukey_FFT_algorithm" title="Cooley-Tukey FFT algorithm" class="mw-redirect">Cooley-Tukey FFT algorithm</a> co-originator <a href="/wiki/John_Wilder_Tukey" title="John Wilder Tukey" class="mw-redirect">John Wilder Tukey</a> '36, Gurney Professor of History and Political Science at Harvard <a href="/wiki/Adam_Ulam" title="Adam Ulam">Adam Ulam</a> '44, physicist <a href="/w/index.php?title=Lewis_Earl_Little&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Lewis Earl Little (page does not exist)">Lewis E. Little</a> '62, <a href="/wiki/Lasker_Award" title="Lasker Award">Lasker Award</a> winning biologist and founder of microbial pathogenesis <a href="/wiki/Stanley_Falkow" title="Stanley Falkow">Stanley Falkow</a> (PhD '59), <a href="/wiki/MIT" title="MIT" class="mw-redirect">MIT</a> neuroscience department chair <a href="/w/index.php?title=Mark_F._Bear&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Mark F. Bear (page does not exist)">Mark F. Bear</a> (B.A. '78, Ph.D '84), <a href="/wiki/University_of_Pennsylvania" title="University of Pennsylvania">Penn</a> psychologist, <a href="/wiki/Lasker_Award" title="Lasker Award">Lasker Award</a> winner and <a href="/wiki/Cognitive_therapy" title="Cognitive therapy">cognitive therapy</a> originator <a href="/wiki/Aaron_Beck" title="Aaron Beck" class="mw-redirect">Aaron Beck</a> '50, <a href="/wiki/John_Bates_Clark_Medal" title="John Bates Clark Medal">John Bates Clark Medal</a> winning <a href="/wiki/MIT" title="MIT" class="mw-redirect">MIT</a> economist <a href="/wiki/Jerry_A._Hausman" title="Jerry A. Hausman">Jerry A. Hausman</a> '68, <a href="/wiki/University_of_Chicago_School_of_Law" title="University of Chicago School of Law" class="mw-redirect">University of Chicago School of Law</a> dean <a href="/wiki/Daniel_Fischel" title="Daniel Fischel">Daniel Fischel</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chicago_Booth" title="Chicago Booth" class="mw-redirect">Chicago Booth</a> economist <a href="/wiki/Randall_Kroszner" title="Randall Kroszner">Randall Kroszner</a> '84, <a href="/wiki/Stanford_Law_School" title="Stanford Law School">Stanford Law School</a> dean <a href="/wiki/Larry_Kramer_(legal_scholar)" title="Larry Kramer (legal scholar)">Larry Kramer (legal scholar)</a>, '80, and <a href="/wiki/Arthur_L._Horwich" title="Arthur L. Horwich">Arthur L. Horwich</a>.</p> 
     <p>Notable past or current faculty have included <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Laureates" title="Nobel Laureates" class="mw-redirect">Nobel Laureates</a> <a href="/wiki/Lars_Onsager" title="Lars Onsager">Lars Onsager</a>, <a href="/wiki/George_Stigler" title="George Stigler">George Stigler</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vernon_L._Smith" title="Vernon L. Smith">Vernon L. Smith</a>, <a href="/wiki/George_Snell" title="George Snell" class="mw-redirect">George Snell</a> and <a href="/wiki/Leon_Cooper" title="Leon Cooper">Leon Cooper</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fields_Medal" title="Fields Medal">Fields Medal</a> winning mathematician <a href="/wiki/David_Mumford" title="David Mumford">David Mumford</a>, mathematician <a href="/wiki/Ulf_Grenander" title="Ulf Grenander">Ulf Grenander</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pulitzer_Prize" title="Pulitzer Prize">Pulitzer Prize</a> winning historian <a href="/wiki/Gordon_S._Wood" title="Gordon S. Wood">Gordon S. Wood</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sakurai_Prize" title="Sakurai Prize">Sakurai Prize</a> winning physicist <a href="/wiki/Gerald_Guralnik" title="Gerald Guralnik">Gerald Guralnik</a> for co-elucidation of the <a href="/wiki/Higgs_mechanism" title="Higgs mechanism">Higgs mechanism</a>, award-winning physicist <a href="/wiki/John_M._Kosterlitz" title="John M. Kosterlitz">John M. Kosterlitz</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Kosterlitz-Thouless_transition" title="Kosterlitz-Thouless transition" class="mw-redirect">Kosterlitz-Thouless transition</a>, computer scientist and inventor of <a href="/wiki/Hypertext" title="Hypertext">hypertext</a> <a href="/wiki/Andries_van_Dam" title="Andries van Dam">Andries van Dam</a>, computer scientist <a href="/wiki/Robert_Sedgewick_(computer_scientist)" title="Robert Sedgewick (computer scientist)">Robert Sedgewick</a>, prominent engineers <a href="/wiki/Daniel_C._Drucker" title="Daniel C. Drucker">Daniel C. Drucker</a>, <a href="/w/index.php?title=L._Ben_Freund&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="L. Ben Freund (page does not exist)">L. Ben Freund</a>, and <a href="/w/index.php?title=Mayo_D._Hersey&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Mayo D. Hersey (page does not exist)">Mayo D. Hersey</a>, <a href="/wiki/BrainGate" title="BrainGate">BrainGate</a> inventor <a href="/w/index.php?title=John_Donoghue_(neuroscientist)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="John Donoghue (neuroscientist) (page does not exist)">John Donoghue</a> (Ph.D 79'), neuroscientist <a href="/w/index.php?title=Mark_F._Bear&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Mark F. Bear (page does not exist)">Mark F. Bear</a> (B.A '78, Ph.D '82), biologist and prominent advocate of biological evolution <a href="/wiki/Kenneth_R._Miller" title="Kenneth R. Miller">Kenneth R. Miller</a>, first president of the <a href="/wiki/American_Sociological_Association" title="American Sociological Association">American Sociological Association</a> <a href="/wiki/Lester_Frank_Ward" title="Lester Frank Ward">Lester Frank Ward</a>, economists <a href="/wiki/Hyman_Minsky" title="Hyman Minsky">Hyman Minsky</a>, Peter MacAvoy, who was a former member of the <a href="/wiki/US_Council_of_Economic_Advisers" title="US Council of Economic Advisers" class="mw-redirect">US Council of Economic Advisers</a>, <a href="/wiki/William_Poole_(economist)" title="William Poole (economist)">William Poole (economist)</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ross_Levine" title="Ross Levine">Ross Levine</a>, <a href="/wiki/Oded_Galor" title="Oded Galor">Oded Galor</a> and <a href="/wiki/Peter_Howitt_(economist)" title="Peter Howitt (economist)">Peter Howitt (economist)</a>, former Prime Minister of Italy and former <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">EU</a> chief <a href="/wiki/Romano_Prodi" title="Romano Prodi">Romano Prodi</a>, former President of Brazil <a href="/wiki/Fernando_Cardoso" title="Fernando Cardoso" class="mw-redirect">Fernando Cardoso</a>, former President of Chile <a href="/wiki/Ricardo_Lagos" title="Ricardo Lagos">Ricardo Lagos</a>, writers <a href="/wiki/Carlos_Fuentes" title="Carlos Fuentes">Carlos Fuentes</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chinua_Achebe" title="Chinua Achebe">Chinua Achebe</a>, <a href="/wiki/Robert_Coover" title="Robert Coover">Robert Coover</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Keith_Waldrop" title="Keith Waldrop">Keith Waldrop</a>, former Presidents of the <a href="/wiki/American_Philosophical_Association" title="American Philosophical Association">American Philosophical Association</a> <a href="/wiki/Jaegwon_Kim" title="Jaegwon Kim">Jaegwon Kim</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ernest_Sosa" title="Ernest Sosa">Ernest Sosa</a>, philosophers <a href="/wiki/Curt_Ducasse" title="Curt Ducasse" class="mw-redirect">Curt Ducasse</a>, <a href="/wiki/Roderick_Chisholm" title="Roderick Chisholm">Roderick Chisholm</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Martha_Nussbaum" title="Martha Nussbaum">Martha Nussbaum</a>, linguist <a href="/wiki/Hans_Kurath" title="Hans Kurath">Hans Kurath</a>, political scientist <a href="/wiki/James_Morone" title="James Morone">James Morone</a> and Senior Fellow <a href="/wiki/Sergei_Khrushchev" title="Sergei Khrushchev">Sergei Khrushchev</a>.</p>
